  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d10b97c7-f28f-4ba6-8ff3-a66b1d7992c2'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer16232201417601099582">In this tense, mesmerizing thriller by Linwood Barclay, critically acclaimed author of Fear the Worst and Too Close to Home, a man’s life unravels around him when the unthinkable strikes.<br/> <br/>A warm summer Saturday. An amusement park. David Harwood is glad to be spending some quality time with his wife, Jan, and their four-year-old son. But what begins as a pleasant family out</span>
  <span id="freeText16232201417601099582" style="display:none">In this tense, mesmerizing thriller by Linwood Barclay, critically acclaimed author of Fear the Worst and Too Close to Home, a man’s life unravels around him when the unthinkable strikes.<br /> <br />A warm summer Saturday. An amusement park. David Harwood is glad to be spending some quality time with his wife, Jan, and their four-year-old son. But what begins as a pleasant family outing turns into a nightmare after an inexplicable disappearance. A frantic search only leads to an even more shocking and harrowing turn of events.<br /> <br />Until this terrifying moment, David Harwood is just a small-town reporter in need of a break. His paper, the Promise Falls Standard, is struggling to survive. Then he gets a lead that just might be the answer to his prayers: a potential scandal involving a controversial development project for the outskirts of this picturesque upstate New York town. It’s a hot-button issue that will surely sell papers and help reverse the Standard’s fortunes, but strangely, David’s editors keep shooting it down. <br /><br />Why?<br /> <br />That’s a question no longer at the top of David’s list. Now the only thing he cares about is restoring his family. Desperate for any clue, David dives into his own investigation—and into a web of lies and deceit. For with every new piece of evidence he uncovers, David finds more questions—and moves ever closer to a shattering truth.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16232201417601099582" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/973975-so-after-reading-broken-promise-and">So, after reading Broken Promise and absolutely loving it like a child, I stumble upon this gem. Reading the summary, I saw David Harwood&#39;s name and then I saw Jan... So I came to a pretty good conclusion that this book will tell me what happened to his wife before The Promise Falls trilogy. So my question is, if I&#39;ve read Broken Promise can I read Never Look Back without being as amazed at the end if I&#39;d not read it?</a>
</div>

<div id="review_221539721" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/221539721" />
    <a title="Arah-Lynda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5859453-arah-lynda"><img alt="Arah-Lynda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601299926p2/5859453.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/221539721?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arah-Lynda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arah-Lynda" href="/user/show/5859453-arah-lynda">Arah-Lynda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5859453-arah-lynda?shelf=top">top</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5859453-arah-lynda?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5859453-arah-lynda?shelf=i-said">i-said</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer221539721" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15624684897899621522">Things are not so good these days for David Harwood.<br/> He cannot seem to nail down a solid lead on a corrupt, privately operated, for- profit prison story that he has been chasing for his local paper in Promise Falls, New York. <br/> His wife Jan has recently been struggling with seriously, severe bouts of depression and has admitted to David that she has even considered suicide. <br/><br/>They definitely could use a break, so spending the day with their four year old son Ethan at a local amusement park, taking </span>
  <span id="freeText15624684897899621522" style="display:none">Things are not so good these days for David Harwood.<br /> He cannot seem to nail down a solid lead on a corrupt, privately operated, for- profit prison story that he has been chasing for his local paper in Promise Falls, New York. <br /> His wife Jan has recently been struggling with seriously, severe bouts of depression and has admitted to David that she has even considered suicide. <br /><br />They definitely could use a break, so spending the day with their four year old son Ethan at a local amusement park, taking time to relax and focus on the good stuff, while enjoying a day of fun and frolic seems to be just the ticket.<br /><br />They have barely made it through the gates though, when things really begin to spin out of control, starting with the disappearance of their son. David and Jan seperate, each of them frantically looking for Ethan, who they had taken their eyes off of for only a split second. Thank God, David soon finds him, unharmed and still asleep in his stroller. As soon as he is certain that Ethan is okay he begins to backtrack to find Jan and let her know......except Jan is not answering her cell and after much searching, waiting, and calling her repeatedly, it begins to dawn on David that she has simply disappeared, vanished into thin air! <br /><br />Let me tell you, I have barely scratched the surface of all the twists, turns and sub-plots in this story of murder and deceipt, corruption and betrayal; that simply roars out of the station at break neck speed and never loses pace, hurtling faster, forward to it's mind-numbing conclusion. <br /><br />This is the second book I have read of Linwood Barclay's and it blew me away! He is absolutely brilliant at writing what I would call, domestic thrillers, with a genuinely, believable cast of characters and unnerving,relatable circumstances that keep you on the edge of your seat. <br /><br />No doubt about it, I am definitley looking for another Linwood Barclay novel. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15624684897899621522" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_217670733" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/217670733" />
    <a title="Patrice Hoffman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5405898-patrice-hoffman"><img alt="Patrice Hoffman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545145717p2/5405898.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/217670733?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrice Hoffman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrice Hoffman" href="/user/show/5405898-patrice-hoffman">Patrice Hoffman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385668040" href="/book/show/7169100-never-look-away">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer217670733" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11815040396904236169">I must be honest, the first <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/458771.Linwood_Barclay' title='Linwood Barclay' rel='nofollow noopener'>Linwood Barclay</a> novel I read did him no justice. I'm glad that this thriller in particular, redeemed the author in my mind. The story begins at an amusement park where a father is one moment sharing special moments with his family, and the next is searching frantically for his missing son. Only to find that son then his world be crumbling again at the disappearance of his wife. David Harwood is a reporter who's currently working on a huge story that could possibly tur</span>
  <span id="freeText11815040396904236169" style="display:none">I must be honest, the first <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/458771.Linwood_Barclay" title="Linwood Barclay" rel="nofollow noopener">Linwood Barclay</a> novel I read did him no justice. I'm glad that this thriller in particular, redeemed the author in my mind. The story begins at an amusement park where a father is one moment sharing special moments with his family, and the next is searching frantically for his missing son. Only to find that son then his world be crumbling again at the disappearance of his wife. David Harwood is a reporter who's currently working on a huge story that could possibly turn things around for the failing town paper he writes for. But, suspiciously his life is turned upside down.<br /><br />Barclay is extremely detailed in his character development. The main cast in this story were given full fleshed out traits and personalities with a past and motivations for the future. I really liked that aspect of this book. I felt I knew these characters and could believe some of their actions. Even the cliched fat cop, the richer than God "antagonist", or the scum-bucket low-life theives all fit and didn't seem too unbelievable. <br /><br />The one thing I did not like about this novel was that I wanted to scream at David Harwood. He was making a lot of dumb mistakes that suspect 101 should know better than to do. I found him to be completely oblivious to his predicament. That was pretty annoying. One other aspect of this novel I didn't like was its predictability. But overall, it's a well written novel and makes anyone think twice about who they're spouse really is or what the people around them could be hiding. I look forward to reading more from this author.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11815040396904236169" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_559017546" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/559017546" />
    <a title="Richard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8386404-richard"><img alt="Richard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351707681p2/8386404.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/559017546?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard" href="/user/show/8386404-richard">Richard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781441804211" href="/book/show/7576678-never-look-away">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8386404-richard?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8386404-richard?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer559017546" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7068771789037145203">7/10<br/><br/>This is the second time I’ve read a Linwood Barclay novel and it seems that he’s got a similar style to that of Harlan Coben (earlier, good Coben, not some of his later bland/unbelievable work) in that there is a mysterious circumstance and then layers upon layers added to shroud that mystery before the inevitable conclusion where it all slots into place. <br/><br/>I like this type of book, admittedly less so now than I used to, as it’s an easy read to get into and run along with. The plot was intrigu</span>
  <span id="freeText7068771789037145203" style="display:none">7/10<br /><br />This is the second time I’ve read a Linwood Barclay novel and it seems that he’s got a similar style to that of Harlan Coben (earlier, good Coben, not some of his later bland/unbelievable work) in that there is a mysterious circumstance and then layers upon layers added to shroud that mystery before the inevitable conclusion where it all slots into place. <br /><br />I like this type of book, admittedly less so now than I used to, as it’s an easy read to get into and run along with. The plot was intriguing in that a man, wife and son go to a theme park for the day and then the wife goes missing. On further inspection it turns out the wife was never at the park. This pipped my interest and was the reason why I chose it as my Audible selection for the month. <br /><br />I’m newish to the Audible bandwagon which is why I chose this sort of novel to ease me into a longer book than those I’d previously listened to coming in at roughly the 13 hour mark compared to the 5 hours of the others I’d done. The narrator initially didn’t do much for me, he was good without excelling but I soon found that things changed and that I really enjoyed the voices he did for certain characters (even the voice of the Detective Duckworth who came across as a drunk stupid Russian even though he really shouldn’t have with him being a sober, clever American and probably wasn’t intending to). By the end it was the narration that was getting me through this more than the plot.<br /><br />The plot, whilst intriguing, soon slipped away after the initial intrigue. By the halfway mark I’d called it and that’s not something I can often boast. I’d figured out the main twists and where it was going to go which sort of defeated the object of this type of book. They’re usually about the chase up to the big reveal. Without the narrator excelling then I could have easily found my attention waning. <br /><br />I’m glad I did this in audiobook but it wasn’t the best thriller out there. It had been on my “wish list” for quite some time now and as a 2016 aim to clear that beast of a list down I thought why not start here. If you’re looking for a complex thriller that leaves you hanging to the end, you may not get what you’re after here. If you’re looking for a decent story with a couple of twists then it’s not a bad shout.<br /><br />If you like this try: “Pines” by Blake Crouch for a mystery that twists until the end.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7068771789037145203" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2107796661" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2107796661" />
    <a title="Dana Moison" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45188714-dana-moison"><img alt="Dana Moison" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1575420980p2/45188714.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2107796661?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dana Moison" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dana Moison" href="/user/show/45188714-dana-moison">Dana Moison</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2107796661" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3233648371050777282">Another great suspense novel by Linwood Barclay! <br/>David Harwood, a journalist who’s struggling to make ends meet, is on an innocent day out with his wife and son at the amusement park. Suddenly his son disappears, and David is afraid he’s been kidnapped. Later on, it appears that his wife, Jan, who was depressed in the last few days, showing suicidal behavior at times, is the one who’s gone missing. David is worried sick about her, but it seems that the police is more disturbed by the suspicious </span>
  <span id="freeText3233648371050777282" style="display:none">Another great suspense novel by Linwood Barclay! <br />David Harwood, a journalist who’s struggling to make ends meet, is on an innocent day out with his wife and son at the amusement park. Suddenly his son disappears, and David is afraid he’s been kidnapped. Later on, it appears that his wife, Jan, who was depressed in the last few days, showing suicidal behavior at times, is the one who’s gone missing. David is worried sick about her, but it seems that the police is more disturbed by the suspicious circumstances of her disappearance and David’s possible involvement. <br />Did some corrupt people caused this tragedy because they wanted to prevent David from publishing a certain story? Who tried to kidnap David’s son? And who is in fact his wife?<br />While there are some questions which is easy for us to answer in the beginning of the story, such as who did what, what is not as clear and makes our imagination work overtime is why they did it. I won’t elaborate on the questions that ran through my mind during the read, to avoid any potentials spoilers, but I’ll admit it took me some time to understand the motives that stood behind the operating characters. It turned out to be a complex and intriguing read. Each time we were introduced to another piece of the puzzle, until finally we could see the whole picture, clearly.<br />I loved reading this book and finished it rather quickly. I would recommend it to all the suspense lovers, and especially readers who are into psychological thrillers!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3233648371050777282" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_89175269" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/89175269" />
    <a title="Melinda Schmidbauer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1744087-melinda-schmidbauer"><img alt="Melinda Schmidbauer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1315827716p2/1744087.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/89175269?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melinda Schmidbauer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melinda Schmidbauer" href="/user/show/1744087-melinda-schmidbauer">Melinda Schmidbauer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Thrillers</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Melinda by: </span>
      LibraryThing Early Release Program
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer89175269" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13570870113486837235">The book starts off with what seems like an innocent trip to the amusement park -- although why anyone would want to take a four-year-old to an amusement park is beyond my comprehension. When Jan and David Harwood's son goes missing at the park, it is the beginning of a chain of events that has David confused about his family, his job and his sanity.<br/><br/>The book sucked me right in, from the first chapter. I received this Friday afternoon, and finished it in less than 24 hours. There are several thin</span>
  <span id="freeText13570870113486837235" style="display:none">The book starts off with what seems like an innocent trip to the amusement park -- although why anyone would want to take a four-year-old to an amusement park is beyond my comprehension. When Jan and David Harwood's son goes missing at the park, it is the beginning of a chain of events that has David confused about his family, his job and his sanity.<br /><br />The book sucked me right in, from the first chapter. I received this Friday afternoon, and finished it in less than 24 hours. There are several things that I really liked about it. First, it appears to be a "stand-alone" novel, not one of a series. While I like series thrillers (Michael Connelly's Bosch books are a good example), I always feel like I have to read the books in order. With stand-alones, I can jump right into an author's newest book, and then look forward to going back to the previous ones if I like this one. I will definitely go back and look up Barclay's newer books!<br /><br />Second, the point of view shifts throughout the book. Normally, I don't like this, but Barclay is very good at handling the alternating first-person chapters, narrated by David, with the other sections told from the points-of-view of David's wife, the investigating police officer, and other characters as needed. The transitions were not jarring at all; I was never confused or thrown out of the story.<br /><br />Lastly, I really liked the font used in this book. Isn't that weird? It isn't something I normally think about, the size and layout of the print seemed really easy to read, even in the low light of the bedroom, or while I was sitting in the brightly lit living room.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13570870113486837235" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_109224573" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/109224573" />
    <a title="Thomas Edmund" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2976142-thomas-edmund"><img alt="Thomas Edmund" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540097981p2/2976142.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/109224573?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas Edmund" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas Edmund" href="/user/show/2976142-thomas-edmund">Thomas Edmund</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer109224573" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7947805422784511740">Never Look Away ranks amongst the best thrillers released this year. While not so deep as to be ever considered literary, the characters of this novel have a realness that is both heart-breaking and frightening.<br/><br/>The story is told by David, a small-time reporter who gets himself mixed up in controversy surrounding the construction of a privately run prison in his home-town of Paradise Falls. After making a few barbed comments to a local politician, the CEO of Star-Spangled Corrections and his hire</span>
  <span id="freeText7947805422784511740" style="display:none">Never Look Away ranks amongst the best thrillers released this year. While not so deep as to be ever considered literary, the characters of this novel have a realness that is both heart-breaking and frightening.<br /><br />The story is told by David, a small-time reporter who gets himself mixed up in controversy surrounding the construction of a privately run prison in his home-town of Paradise Falls. After making a few barbed comments to a local politician, the CEO of Star-Spangled Corrections and his hired thug pay David a private visit that leaves him wondering if he’s bitten off more than he can chew.<br /><br />As if that wasn’t enough David’s wife Jan begins to show signs of depression, and while there is a twist on this later I found this sequence of events particularly heart-renching.<br /><br />The real action begins when Jan and her work-mate disappear and an official police investigation is launched with David as the prime-suspect. Caught between corrupt politicians, a suspicious and stubborn detective, David struggles to deal with the disappearance of his wife and destruction of his life as he knew it.<br /><br />So while the characters are well thought out and the plotline is intelligence Never Look Away has some imperfections – some of the characters are a hairsbreadth away from stereotypeland and there are aspects of the wife’s disappearance which (aside from being hard to explain without spoilers) are a little theme-less, uninteresting and hard to fully reconcile with the overall storyline.<br /><br />Perhaps it’s hard to grasp what the heck I mean here so I’d be interested in hearing what other readers have to say about it... <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7947805422784511740" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_427091447" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/427091447" />
    <a title="Simón" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11159809-sim-n"><img alt="Simón" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1342903312p2/11159809.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/427091447?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simón" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simón" href="/user/show/11159809-sim-n">Simón</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer427091447" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13423165347064670672">What qualities do you look for in a novel? If any of the below fill you with joy and excitement, then this is the book for you!<br/><br/>1. Prose that is so truly prosaic I hoped and suspected it was an intentional parody (apparently it was not).<br/>2. Dialogue so awkward and unpersuasive that it felt like a poorly dubbed movie.<br/>3. Characters so stilted they were surely off-cuts from Geppetto's workshop.<br/>4. Situations and plot-twists so contrived (even by cheap airport thriller standards) you begin to wonder if</span>
  <span id="freeText13423165347064670672" style="display:none">What qualities do you look for in a novel? If any of the below fill you with joy and excitement, then this is the book for you!<br /><br />1. Prose that is so truly prosaic I hoped and suspected it was an intentional parody (apparently it was not).<br />2. Dialogue so awkward and unpersuasive that it felt like a poorly dubbed movie.<br />3. Characters so stilted they were surely off-cuts from Geppetto's workshop.<br />4. Situations and plot-twists so contrived (even by cheap airport thriller standards) you begin to wonder if it's a Benny Hill farce.<br /><br />In closing, I would like to thank Mr Linwood Barclay for doubling my appreciation of literary finesse, intimately drawn psychological portraits, and the power of great fiction to turn a mirror to one's very soul.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1076047944" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1076047944" />
    <a title="Rick Urban" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5981340-rick-urban"><img alt="Rick Urban" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312728082p2/5981340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1076047944?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rick Urban" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rick Urban" href="/user/show/5981340-rick-urban">Rick Urban</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1076047944" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10694323051671753986">"Gone Girl" without the psychological acuity that Gillian Flynn brings to her writing. In fact, there is an air of unreality to the entire book that makes this seem like those CBS tv shows where you know that the characters are just that...fictional characters you would never see in the real world. Which is fine...this is a thriller, and on those terms, it's very entertaining. All the loose threads are tied up at the end, karma gets who it is supposed to, etc. etc. <br/><br/>Now let's talk about the Steph</span>
  <span id="freeText10694323051671753986" style="display:none">"Gone Girl" without the psychological acuity that Gillian Flynn brings to her writing. In fact, there is an air of unreality to the entire book that makes this seem like those CBS tv shows where you know that the characters are just that...fictional characters you would never see in the real world. Which is fine...this is a thriller, and on those terms, it's very entertaining. All the loose threads are tied up at the end, karma gets who it is supposed to, etc. etc. <br /><br />Now let's talk about the Stephen King blurbs about this book: on the cover, it says "The best thriller I've read in five years", and elsewhere he says that the twists are wholly unexpected. As much as I love the man's writing, and I do love it a lot, let this be a warning to those of you out there who pay attention to these things: you cannot believe Stephen King's blurbs! The man is absolutely shameless in over-hyping both other people's projects as well as his own (he is still beating the drum for the tv series of his book Under the Dome, which is one of the stupidest, most lazily written and acted shows on television). And to say that in FIVE YEARS of thrillers being published from around the world, this is the BEST, is hyperbole of the highest order. I know someone will say he's only talking about thrillers HE has read, but this man reads like most people breathe, so it's unbelievable to me that he could rank this book so highly...practically any Michael Connelly book trumps it, just for one example. And perhaps I was predisposed to look for "twists" after his discussion of them, but I'd say 80% of the plot twists were easily deduced ahead of time. So, enjoy the book, it's a fun ride, but don't let Mr. King's exaggerated praise get your hope TOO high... </span>
  <a data-text-id="10694323051671753986" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer930817066" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6390616974697556755">Wow. What happened?<br/><br/>Linwood Barkley is brilliant at coming up with convoluted plots and slowly peeling the layers back, slowly bringing the reader out from a state of unknowing one little reveal at a time.<br/>And his characters are quite well drawn. I got quite a kick out of the protagonist's dad, who, I'm embarrassed to say, reminds me a little of myself. No, I haven't made those traffic signs, but it has occurred to me once in a while.<br/><br/>But what happened? Did he hand off the writing duties to some ki</span>
  <span id="freeText6390616974697556755" style="display:none">Wow. What happened?<br /><br />Linwood Barkley is brilliant at coming up with convoluted plots and slowly peeling the layers back, slowly bringing the reader out from a state of unknowing one little reveal at a time.<br />And his characters are quite well drawn. I got quite a kick out of the protagonist's dad, who, I'm embarrassed to say, reminds me a little of myself. No, I haven't made those traffic signs, but it has occurred to me once in a while.<br /><br />But what happened? Did he hand off the writing duties to some kid for the last 50 pages or so?<br />Suddenly the dialogue became inane, and there was one plot development that defied reason so badly that I almost couldn't finish it.<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />Gretchen. Really? Kidnap a kid to get back at the wife (30 years later, mind you) of a guy who's going through the worst hell of his life? Who you had offered a night's stay and nice breakfast because you felt sorry for him? Nice that you were so kind to the lad, though. That's sweet. All is forgiven.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Sorry. I can't buy any of that. Even fiction needs to adhere to some understandable human behavior.<br />I will read him again because other than that gap of believability, he is a pretty skilled plot master. But jeez.<br /></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2548223871" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15228689131678738811">4 Stars. A little predictable as things turn from bad to much worse for David Harwood. But it catches you in a vulnerable place! His wife Jan wanted to have a family day and bought tickets to the local amusement park. Along with their adorable four-year-old Ethan, they're off to ride the roller coasters. In the park their son goes missing, but he's soon found. Now his wife is missing, not to be found in ten minutes like Ethan. David is desperate but everything he has done over the last few days,</span>
  <span id="freeText15228689131678738811" style="display:none">4 Stars. A little predictable as things turn from bad to much worse for David Harwood. But it catches you in a vulnerable place! His wife Jan wanted to have a family day and bought tickets to the local amusement park. Along with their adorable four-year-old Ethan, they're off to ride the roller coasters. In the park their son goes missing, but he's soon found. Now his wife is missing, not to be found in ten minutes like Ethan. David is desperate but everything he has done over the last few days, everything he has experienced over the last few weeks, now says something different in the light of his wife being missing. Especially to the police. We all know the spouse is the first suspect. Harwood is a reporter for the local rag, the Promise Falls Standard, which is spiralling downward - like all papers. Does Jan's predicament have anything to do with Harwood's potential story about City Hall corruption surrounding a proposal for a new private prison in town? What does the title mean? Ethan did disappear when Jan took her eyes away for a few minutes. Or is it something else? How can anyone not look away if only for a minute? (October 2018)</span>

<div id="review_1387897801" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1387897801" />
    <a title="CD {Boulder Blvd}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31857175-cd-boulder-blvd"><img alt="CD {Boulder Blvd}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413765420p2/31857175.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1387897801?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="CD {Boulder Blvd}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="CD {Boulder Blvd}" href="/user/show/31857175-cd-boulder-blvd">CD {Boulder Blvd}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31857175-cd-boulder-blvd?shelf=pov-1st-person-ugh">pov-1st-person-ugh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31857175-cd-boulder-blvd?shelf=thriller-suspense-mystery">thriller-suspense-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31857175-cd-boulder-blvd?shelf=s-bv-library">s-bv-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31857175-cd-boulder-blvd?shelf=pov-changing-ugh">pov-changing-ugh</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1387897801" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6359390683603578343">I have a love/hate relationship with Linwood Barclay's books. It's like I can feel the potential could be there, it just doesn't materialize. I started reading Oct 20 and was having a hard time for the first 25% of the book I was pretty bored and not pulled into the plot. Although I wanted to find out what happened to Dave's wife, it was difficult to wade through all the details he drops which he may pick up at a later point.<br/><br/>Then this week, I decided to push through and get this book off my "cur</span>
  <span id="freeText6359390683603578343" style="display:none">I have a love/hate relationship with Linwood Barclay's books. It's like I can feel the potential could be there, it just doesn't materialize. I started reading Oct 20 and was having a hard time for the first 25% of the book I was pretty bored and not pulled into the plot. Although I wanted to find out what happened to Dave's wife, it was difficult to wade through all the details he drops which he may pick up at a later point.<br /><br />Then this week, I decided to push through and get this book off my "currently reading" list. I knew if I got far enough into the story that I would be able to get this finished. The book uses a 3rd person and a 1st person narrative which I'm not too fond of. When the story is centered on Dave, the reporter, it's in 1st person. When the police are pulling the threads of his missing wife together and they are leading to him as a prime suspect, the story actually gets frustrating, not interesting. In 1st POV, his frustration with the situation is coming through, but then it just made it frustrating to read.<br /><br />None of the characters are very likable or interesting and it's hard to be concerned about them. In fact, most of the characters I didn't like. Dave, the main character got on my nerves with constantly doing the opposite of what he should do. The bad guys are TV cliche bad guys.<br /><br />There were some elements of the plot I really liked, but it got lost in all the meanderings the plot took. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6359390683603578343" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2065514-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442612806p2/2065514.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/80021483?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/2065514-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2065514-michael?shelf=advanced-copy-review">advanced-copy-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2065514-michael?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2065514-michael?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2065514-michael?shelf=action-thriller">action-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2065514-michael?shelf=new-york-times-best-seller">new-york-times-best-seller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2065514-michael?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2065514-michael?shelf=reader-s-club-review-request">reader-s-club-review-request</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2065514-michael?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2065514-michael?shelf=amature-detective">amature-detective</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer80021483" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12584805588624516979">David Harwood, reporter, has been working on a story of Star Spangled Corrections. They are a private correctional corporation and want to build a prison in his town. David has records of payoffs of politicians by the president of the corporation but David's editors delay in publishing it.<br/><br/>One day, David goes to Five Mountains amusement park with his wife,Jan, and their four year old son, Ethan. As they approach the park enterence, Jan remembers her back pak and returns to the car, telling her hu</span>
  <span id="freeText12584805588624516979" style="display:none">David Harwood, reporter, has been working on a story of Star Spangled Corrections. They are a private correctional corporation and want to build a prison in his town. David has records of payoffs of politicians by the president of the corporation but David's editors delay in publishing it.<br /><br />One day, David goes to Five Mountains amusement park with his wife,Jan, and their four year old son, Ethan. As they approach the park enterence, Jan remembers her back pak and returns to the car, telling her husband that she'll meet him inside.<br /><br />David waits but Jan never appears.<br /><br />He begins a search and notifies park security. When the search is unsuccessful, park officials check security cameras of people entering the park but there is no record of Jan's enterance.<br /><br />Local police begin their investigation and find that the tickets were purchased on line but that only two tickets were purchased. Now, the lead detective believes that David may have caused his wife's disappearance.<br /><br />David conducts his own search and discovers that many of the things that he and his wife built their lives around were falsehoods. Ethan keeps asking for his mother, David needs to find her and learn why she deceived him.<br /><br />As a character, David is most sympathetic. His plight is tragic but the reader also learns what his wife is doing and wonders why David, a reporter, couldn't see things as they really were. Jan is a true Machiavellian, out for herself. She's a truly unlikable person and this makes the readers empathy for David even greater.<br /><br />The plot is magnificant. Barclay is like a master fisherman, casting his lines in different directions and then reeling them back with a story that catches the reader's breath.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12584805588624516979" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText13201892069753155196" style="display:none">I was extremely hesitant in picking this book up to start with, I didn't like the fact that it was such a long book and the writing was tiny. <br /><br />Furthermore, turns out this book was great! I am so happy I picked it up :)<br /><br />After I eventually got past the confusion of it at the beginning. To be honest, I was actually going to put this book down and pick up another I was so confused and I didn't exactly admire the writing style. However, Once I got past that and got used to the writing style it then eventually became a very interesting read. So much that I couldn't put it down. I thoroughly enjoyed the book in the end. <br /><br />I have a lot of theories whilst reading this and the more I read it the more the theories I had got crushed and broken and something else happened that I wasn't expecting. It was quite a fast past moving book. <br /><br />I really recommend it :)</span>

<div id="review_106255905" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/106255905" />
    <a title="Denise" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2657711-denise"><img alt="Denise" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1405745990p2/2657711.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/106255905?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Denise" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Denise" href="/user/show/2657711-denise">Denise</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer106255905" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15365997033628200098"> Do you really know the ones you love?, February 13, 2010 <br/>I have read all of Linwood Barclay's back-list and I must say that this one is better than the last two and I'm relieved that he's pulled back a little with the unbelievable endings and returned to writing a taut mystery thriller that is both fast paced and suspenseful. I found both Fear the Worst: A Thriller and Too Close to Home: A Thriller to be just way too over the top and am glad that Barclay has returned to a style similar to the o</span>
  <span id="freeText15365997033628200098" style="display:none"> Do you really know the ones you love?, February 13, 2010 <br />I have read all of Linwood Barclay's back-list and I must say that this one is better than the last two and I'm relieved that he's pulled back a little with the unbelievable endings and returned to writing a taut mystery thriller that is both fast paced and suspenseful. I found both Fear the Worst: A Thriller and Too Close to Home: A Thriller to be just way too over the top and am glad that Barclay has returned to a style similar to the one used with what I consider to be my favorite of his novels, No Time for Goodbye. Yeah, all his books require a bit of suspension of disbelief at the scenarios, but the main character -- almost consistently a family man with a wife and child -- is usually a sympathetic protagonist and one whom you want to see get to the bottom of the mystery. <br /><br />In this novel, newspaper reporter David Harwood is investigating what might be corruption with regard to a new privatized prison that is being hawked as the next best thing for the small town of Promise Falls, New York. He's married to Jan and they have a 4 year old son named Ethan. One day, while they're at an amusement park, one of them disappears!! David races from place to place to figure out what is going on and, although several subplots are brewing simultaneously, the energy and the narrative keep the reader glued to the pages. Even though the reader knows what is happening and why, it's a fun romp to the end. <br /><br />If you like a good mystery thriller, you'll enjoy this one. Recommend.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15365997033628200098" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer102974050" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13097491127330025470">Oh, what a wonderful writer! I just loved this book! A very unpredictable plot and just terrific characters. There was a hint of Barclay's old star, Zack Walker, in this main character's father (those driving cards, ha!). Really, this was a spectacular mystery, told with Barclay's characteristic flair and sense of humour. I really enjoyed reading it, and it will be a long wait until his next mystery comes out!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1087371313" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1087371313" />
    <a title="Siobhan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35855553-siobhan"><img alt="Siobhan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510311895p2/35855553.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1087371313?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Siobhan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Siobhan" href="/user/show/35855553-siobhan">Siobhan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780752883366" href="/book/show/7781378-never-look-away">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1087371313" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4397993710624882635">I will be the first to admit that Linwood Barclay books often connect storylines together, creating something intricate, in a way that is totally unbelievable. I’m more than aware that some people have given up with him for this very reason, but for me I enjoy this factor. For me Barclay is a nice change to the much darker crime books I read by Sharon Bolton, Mo Hayder and Karin Slaughter to name but three. For me, therefore, Barclay books are a nice break away from the grittier crime books out </span>
  <span id="freeText4397993710624882635" style="display:none">I will be the first to admit that Linwood Barclay books often connect storylines together, creating something intricate, in a way that is totally unbelievable. I’m more than aware that some people have given up with him for this very reason, but for me I enjoy this factor. For me Barclay is a nice change to the much darker crime books I read by Sharon Bolton, Mo Hayder and Karin Slaughter to name but three. For me, therefore, Barclay books are a nice break away from the grittier crime books out there.<br /><br />Never Look Away starts off as a story where you think Barclay may be avoiding his usual flare, going for a story that is no more complex than a missing woman. Once you get part way through, however, other storylines are mixed in. As always with Barclay, he manages to combine these different storylines in a wonderful way, creating a multi-layered story that keeps you engaged throughout. We find ourselves interested in not only one crime but in multiple as we try to understand how everything goes together in this wacky idea.<br /><br />Whilst not my favourite Barclay book, it was still a good read. I felt as though the ending was a bit quick, as though he brought things together all of a sudden as he realised he would soon be making the book much longer than was necessary, but that is my only real problem with the book. Had the ending been better fleshed out I probably would have been happier with it.<br /><br />Overall, a typically enjoyable Barclay read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4397993710624882635" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/344129847?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly" href="/user/show/8545345-kelly">Kelly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780752883366" href="/book/show/7781378-never-look-away">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8545345-kelly?shelf=crime-thrillers-and-mystery">crime-thrillers-and-mystery</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer344129847" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12645239273277916157">I try to avoid novels which see the lead character accused of a crime and fighting to clear their name, largely because they make my blood pressure rise in annoyance at the 'coincidences' which are oh so obvious and yet other characters cannot see them. This attitude made me dislike this book before I had even started, but I was proven wrong. The interweaving of the past and present lives of Jan Harwood connected many of the plot points nicely throughout the novel leaving for some shock twists a</span>
  <span id="freeText12645239273277916157" style="display:none">I try to avoid novels which see the lead character accused of a crime and fighting to clear their name, largely because they make my blood pressure rise in annoyance at the 'coincidences' which are oh so obvious and yet other characters cannot see them. This attitude made me dislike this book before I had even started, but I was proven wrong. The interweaving of the past and present lives of Jan Harwood connected many of the plot points nicely throughout the novel leaving for some shock twists and adding realistic layers to the plot. <br />The coincidences and evidence pointing toward David as the kidnapper/murderer were made more believable by Detective Duckworth who was inclined to believe David in some aspects of the investigation and was not condemning him from the start which would have been frustrating.<br /><br />Despite my initial reservations I was really glad that I continued to read this book and will definitely be reading more by the author! </span>
  <a data-text-id="12645239273277916157" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1243101512" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1243101512" />
    <a title="Cheryl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22026875-cheryl"><img alt="Cheryl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373374354p2/22026875.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1243101512?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cheryl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cheryl" href="/user/show/22026875-cheryl">Cheryl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553591743" href="/book/show/9403077-never-look-away">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1243101512" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4034563167780885397">This was hard to rate. The first half of the book gets 3 stars. The second half gets 2 stars. So, really a 2 and 1/2 stars total. At least I finished this book, unlike Too Close to Home. The author uses Harlan Coben-like plots, but doesn't write as well as Coben. This book lagged in the middle, and really could've been 100 pages shorter. Not very deep character development, and the twists were kind of predictable. Get it at the library, but don't buy it. </span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7JTmbq3ObZnaqDo8zkn+IlMLF6ILlkRn56NTTMS8hlPeWlGkK+3ITfv1QUo3FDiuhlDnMUaLExfv9CN2S2L6ZQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wBuG9f7DakpYspTixGmTdPII3p+u3XzCzJ4PdjS7SRfy1TE/eODPnnnv75Q9NFX4J1MuDOPAK7LEyX9Mu2U1IQ==')})
  }

//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_7775815'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7775815-lipstick-in-afghanistan?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Lipstick in Afghanistan<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/3390616.Roberta_Gately?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Roberta Gately<\/a><span title=\"Goodreads Author!\">*<\/span>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.65 avg rating &mdash; 1,422 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2010\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer9987944834972541941\">Roberta Gately’s lyrical and authentic debut novel—inspired by her own experiences as a nurse in third world war zones—is one woman’s moving story of offering help and finding hope in the last place she expected. Gripped by haunting magazine images o<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText9987944834972541941\" style=\"display:none\">Roberta Gately’s lyrical and authentic debut novel—inspired by her own experiences as a nurse in third world war zones—is one woman’s moving story of offering help and finding hope in the last place she expected. Gripped by haunting magazine images of starving refugees, Elsa has dreamed of becoming a nurse since she was a teenager. Of leaving her humble working-class Boston neighborhood to help people whose lives are far more difficult than her own. No one in her family has ever escaped poverty, but Elsa has a secret weapon: a tube of lipstick she found in her older sister’s bureau. Wearing it never fails to raise her spirits and cement her determination. With lipstick on, she can do anything—even travel alone to war-torn Afghanistan in the wake of 9/11. But violent nights as an ER nurse in South Boston could not prepare Elsa for the devastation she witnesses at the small medical clinic she runs in Bamiyan. As she struggles to prove herself to the Afghan doctors and local villagers, she begins a forbidden romance with her only confidant, a charming Special Forces soldier. Then, a tube of lipstick she finds in the aftermath of a tragic bus bombing leads her to another life-changing friendship. In her neighbor Parween, Elsa finds a kindred spirit, fiery and generous. Together, the two women risk their lives to save friends and family from the worst excesses of the Taliban. But when the war waging around them threatens their own survival, Elsa discovers her only hope is to unveil the warrior within. Roberta Gately’s raw, intimate novel is an unforgettable tribute to the power of friendship and a poignant reminder of the tragic cost of war.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"9987944834972541941\"           $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_7932168').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_7932168').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/458771.Linwood_Barclay">About Linwood Barclay</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/458771.Linwood_Barclay"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1418584169p3/458771.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/458771.Linwood_Barclay">Linwood Barclay
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
4,318
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4001116788193645861">Linwood Barclay is the #1 internationally bestselling author of seventeen novels for adults, including No Time for Goodbye, Trust Your Eyes and, most recently, A Noise Downstairs. He has also written two novels for children and screenplays.<br/>Three of those seventeen novels comprise the epic Promise Falls trilogy: Broken Promise, Far From True, and The Twenty-Three. His two novels for children – Chas</span>
  <span id="freeText4001116788193645861" style="display:none">Linwood Barclay is the #1 internationally bestselling author of seventeen novels for adults, including No Time for Goodbye, Trust Your Eyes and, most recently, A Noise Downstairs. He has also written two novels for children and screenplays.<br />Three of those seventeen novels comprise the epic Promise Falls trilogy: Broken Promise, Far From True, and The Twenty-Three. His two novels for children – Chase and Escape – star a computer-enhanced dog named Chipper who’s on the run from the evil organization that turned him into a super-pup. <br />Barclay’s 2011 thriller, The Accident, has been turned into the six-part television series L’Accident in France, and he adapted his novel Never Saw it Coming for the movie, directed by Gail Harvey and starring Eric Roberts and Emily Hampshire. Several of his other books either have been, or still are, in development for TV and film.<br />After spending his formative years helping run a cottage resort and trailer park after his father died when he was 16, Barclay got his first newspaper job at the Peterborough Examiner, a small Ontario daily. In 1981, he joined the Toronto Star, Canada’s largest circulation newspaper.<br />He held such positions as assistant city editor, chief copy editor, news editor, and Life section editor, before becoming the paper’s humour columnist in 1993. He was one of the paper’s most popular columnists before retiring from the position in 2008 to work exclusively on books.<br />In 2004, he launched his mystery series about an anxiety-ridden, know-it-all, pain-in-the-butt father by the name of Zack Walker. Bad Move, the first book, was followed by three more Zack Walker thrillers: Bad Guys, Lone Wolf, and Stone Rain. (The last two were published in the UK under the titles Bad Luck and Bad News.)<br />His first standalone thriller, No Time for Goodbye, was published in 2007 to critical acclaim and great international success. The following year, it was a Richard and Judy Summer Read selection in the UK, and did seven straight weeks at #1 on the UK bestseller list, and finished 2008 as the top selling novel of the year there. The book has since been sold around the world and been translated into nearly thirty languages.<br />Barclay was born in the United States but moved to Canada just before turning four years old when his father, a commercial artist whose illustrations of cars appeared in Life, Look and Saturday Evening Post (before photography took over), accepted a position with an advertising agency north of the border. Barclay, who graduated with an English literature degree from Trent University, in Peterborough, Ontario, was fortunate to have some very fine mentors; in particular, the celebrated Canadian author Margaret Laurence, whom Linwood first met when she served as writer-in-residence at Trent, and Kenneth Millar, who, under the name Ross Macdonald, wrote the acclaimed series of mystery novels featuring detective Lew Archer. It was at Trent that he met Neetha, the woman who would become his wife. They have two grown children, Spencer and Paige.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4001116788193645861" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

He was a relentless putterer, always looking for something to fix or tear down and do all over again. A door or cupboard hinge never had a chance to squeak twice. Dad practically carried a can of WD-40 with him at all times. A stuck window, a dripping tap, a running toilet, a jiggly doorknob—none of them stood a chance in our house. Dad always knew exactly what tool he needed, and could have strolled into his garage blindfolded to lay his hands on it.&rdquo;</span>
